$fesken/vi-m_FESK+IN $/vi-m_+IN\n
{="swaddle?". Millett (1982) following Colborn (1940) suggests a\n
miswriting in the common exemplar of S for R and emends to FERKIN < OE\n
fercian. This usually means "convey, bring" but is attested in OE with\n
the meanings "support, feed". I think it unlikely, however, that the scribes\n
of both  B and T would have perpetuated such a mistake. I favour MED\'s\n
reading, which invokes Latin fasciare and OF faissier "swaddle". Godefroy\n
lists among the many attested forms for the related noun faisse, the variant\n
fesche. A form *fescher could be Anglicised as FESKIN in early Middle\n
English, cf. "task" < OF tasche=}\n
